<p><b>Erfurt</b> (<small>German pronunciation:</small> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[ˈɛʁfʊʁt]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:De-Erfurt.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3e/De-Erfurt.ogg" class="internal" title="De-Erfurt.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup>) is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_(political)" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital (political)">capital</a> and largest city in the state of <a href="/wiki/Thuringia" title="Thuringia">Thuringia</a>, central Germany. It lies in the southern part of the <a href="/wiki/Thuringian_Basin" title="Thuringian Basin">Thuringian Basin</a>, within the wide valley of the <a href="/wiki/Gera_(river)" title="Gera (river)">Gera river</a>. It is located 100&#160;km (62&#160;mi) south-west of <a href="/wiki/Leipzig" title="Leipzig">Leipzig</a>, 300&#160;km (186&#160;mi) south-west of <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, 400&#160;km (249&#160;mi) north of <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> and 250&#160;km (155&#160;mi) north-east of <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>. Together with neighbouring cities <a href="/wiki/Weimar" title="Weimar">Weimar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jena" title="Jena">Jena</a> it forms the central metropolitan area of Thuringia with approximately 500,000 inhabitants.</p>
<p>Erfurt's old town is one of the most intact medieval cities in Germany,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> having survived <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> with very little damage. Tourist attractions include the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Kr%C3%A4merbr%C3%BCcke" title="Krämerbrücke">Krämerbrücke</a></span> (Merchants' bridge), the ensemble of <a href="/wiki/Erfurt_Cathedral" title="Erfurt Cathedral">Erfurt Cathedral</a> and <i>Severikirche</i> (St Severus's Church) and Petersburg Citadel, one of the largest and best preserved town fortresses in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The city's economy is based on agriculture, horticulture and microelectronics. Its central location has led to it becoming a logistics hub for Germany and central Europe. Erfurt hosts the second-largest trade fair in eastern Germany (after Leipzig) as well as the public television children’s channel <a href="/wiki/KiKa" title="KiKa">KiKa</a>.</p>
<p>The city is situated on the <a href="/wiki/Via_Regia" title="Via Regia">Via Regia</a>, a medieval trade and pilgrims' road network. Modern day Erfurt is also a hub for <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" title="Intercity-Express">ICE</a> high speed trains and other German and European transport networks. Erfurt was first mentioned in 742, as <a href="/wiki/Saint_Boniface" title="Saint Boniface">Saint Boniface</a> founded the diocese. Although the town did not belong to any of the Thuringian states politically, it quickly became the economic centre of the region. It was part of the <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Mainz" title="Electorate of Mainz">Electorate of Mainz</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, and later became part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Kingdom of Prussia</a> in 1802. From 1949 until 1990 Erfurt was part of the <a href="/wiki/German_Democratic_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="German Democratic Republic">German Democratic Republic</a> (East Germany).</p>
<p>Notable institutions in Erfurt are the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Labour_Court_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Labour Court of Germany">Federal Labour Court of Germany</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Erfurt" title="University of Erfurt">University of Erfurt</a> and the <i>Fachhochschule Erfurt</i> (University of Applied Sciences).</p>
<p>The university was founded in 1379,<sup id="cite_ref-uni-erfurt.de_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uni-erfurt.de-4">[4]</a></sup> making it the first university to be established within the geographic area which constitutes modern-day Germany. It closed in 1816 and was re-established in 1994, with the main modern campus on what was a former teachers' training college. <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> (1483 - 1546) was the most famous student of the institution, studying there from 1501.<sup id="cite_ref-uni-erfurt.de_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uni-erfurt.de-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other famous Erfurters include the medieval philosopher and mystic <a href="/wiki/Meister_Eckhart" title="Meister Eckhart">Meister Eckhart</a> (c. 1260-1328), the Baroque composer <a href="/wiki/Johann_Pachelbel" title="Johann Pachelbel">Johann Pachelbel</a> (1653-1706), the sociologist <a href="/wiki/Max_Weber" title="Max Weber">Max Weber</a> (1864-1920), rapper <a href="/wiki/Clueso" title="Clueso">Clueso</a> (Thomas Hübner) (1980-), and <a href="/wiki/Gunda_Niemann" class="mw-redirect" title="Gunda Niemann">Gunda Niemann</a> (1966- ), three-times Olympic speed skating gold-medal winner.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Erfurt" title="Timeline of Erfurt">Timeline of Erfurt</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory_and_antiquity">Prehistory and antiquity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Prehistory and antiquity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Erfurt is an old <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic settlement</a>. The earliest evidence of human settlement dates from the prehistoric era; archaeological finds from the north of Erfurt revealed human traces from the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">paleolithic</a> period, ca. 100,000 BCE<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Melchendorf&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Melchendorf (page does not exist)">Melchendorf</a> dig in the southern city part showed a settlement from the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_period" class="mw-redirect" title="Neolithic period">neolithic period</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[note 1]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Thuringii" title="Thuringii">Thuringii</a> inhabited the Erfurt area ca. 480 and gave their name to Thuringia ca. 500.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schedel_erfurt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Schedel_erfurt.jpg/220px-Schedel_erfurt.jpg" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Schedel_erfurt.jpg/330px-Schedel_erfurt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Schedel_erfurt.jpg/440px-Schedel_erfurt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="1079" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schedel_erfurt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Erfurt, woodcut from the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Chronicle" title="Nuremberg Chronicle">Nuremberg Chronicle</a>, 1493</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alte_Synagoge_Erfurt.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Alte_Synagoge_Erfurt.JPG/220px-Alte_Synagoge_Erfurt.JPG" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Alte_Synagoge_Erfurt.JPG/330px-Alte_Synagoge_Erfurt.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Alte_Synagoge_Erfurt.JPG/440px-Alte_Synagoge_Erfurt.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1480" data-file-height="1205" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alte_Synagoge_Erfurt.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Old_Synagogue_(Erfurt)" title="Old Synagogue (Erfurt)">Old synagogue</a>, the oldest in Europe (1094)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CollegiumMaius.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/CollegiumMaius.jpg/220px-CollegiumMaius.jpg" width="220" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/CollegiumMaius.jpg/330px-CollegiumMaius.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/CollegiumMaius.jpg/440px-CollegiumMaius.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1156" data-file-height="1030" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CollegiumMaius.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Collegium maius building of the old university (1392)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The town is first mentioned in 742 under the name of "Erphesfurt": in that year, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Boniface" title="Saint Boniface">Saint Boniface</a> wrote to <a href="/wiki/Pope_Zachary" title="Pope Zachary">Pope Zachary</a> to inform him that he had established three <a href="/wiki/Diocese" title="Diocese">dioceses</a> in central Germany, one of them "in a place called Erphesfurt, which for a long time has been inhabited by pagan natives." All three dioceses (the other two were <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrzburg" title="Würzburg">Würzburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/B%C3%BCraburg" title="Büraburg">Büraburg</a>) were confirmed by Zachary the next year, though in 755 Erfurt was brought into the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Mainz" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Mainz">diocese of Mainz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> That the place was populous already is borne out by archeological evidence, which includes 23 graves and six horse burials from the sixth and seventh centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Throughout the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, Erfurt was an important trading town because of its location, near a <a href="/wiki/Ford_(river)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford (river)">ford</a> across the Gera river. Together with the other five Thuringian <a href="/wiki/Woad" class="mw-redirect" title="Woad">woad</a> towns of <a href="/wiki/Gotha_(town)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gotha (town)">Gotha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bad_Tennstedt" title="Bad Tennstedt">Tennstedt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arnstadt" title="Arnstadt">Arnstadt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bad_Langensalza" title="Bad Langensalza">Langensalza</a> it was the centre of the German woad trade, which made those cities very wealthy. Erfurt was the junction of important trade routes: the <a href="/wiki/Via_Regia" title="Via Regia">Via Regia</a> was one of the most used east–west roads between France and Russia (via <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, Erfurt, <a href="/wiki/Leipzig" title="Leipzig">Leipzig</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Wrocław">Wrocław</a>) and another route in north–south direction was the connection between the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> ports (e. g. <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCbeck" title="Lübeck">Lübeck</a>) and the potent upper Italian city-states like <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>.</p>
<p>During the 10th and 11th centuries both the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Emperor</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Mainz" title="Electorate of Mainz">Electorate of Mainz</a> held some privileges in Erfurt. The German kings had an important monastery on Petersberg hill and the Archbishops of Mainz collected taxes from the people. Around 1100, some people became free citizens by paying the annual "<span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Freizins</span>" (liberation tax), which marks a first step in becoming an independent city. During the 12th century, as a sign of more and more independence, the citizens built a city wall around Erfurt (in the area of today's <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Juri-Gagarin-Ring</span>). After 1200, independence was fulfilled and a city council was founded in 1217; the town hall was built in 1275. In the following decades, the council bought a city-owned territory around Erfurt which consisted at its height of nearly 100 villages and castles and even another small town (<a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6mmerda" title="Sömmerda">Sömmerda</a>). Erfurt became an important regional power between the <a href="/wiki/Landgraviate_of_Thuringia" class="mw-redirect" title="Landgraviate of Thuringia">Landgraviate of Thuringia</a> around, the Electorate of Mainz to the west and the <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Saxony" title="Electorate of Saxony">Electorate of Saxony</a> to the east. Between 1306 and 1481, Erfurt was allied with the two other major Thuringian cities (<a href="/wiki/M%C3%BChlhausen" title="Mühlhausen">Mühlhausen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nordhausen" title="Nordhausen">Nordhausen</a>) in the Thuringian City Alliance and the three cities joined the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a> together in 1430. A peak in economic development was reached in the 15th century, when the city had a population of 20,000 making it to one of the largest in Germany. Between 1432 and 1446, a second and higher city wall was established. In 1483, a first city fortress was built on <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cyriaksburg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cyriaksburg (page does not exist)">Cyriaksburg</a> hill in the southwestern part of the town.</p>
<p>The Jewish community of Erfurt was founded in the 11th century and became, together with <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Worms,_Germany" title="Worms, Germany">Worms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Speyer" title="Speyer">Speyer</a>, one of the most influential in Germany. Their <a href="/wiki/Old_Synagogue_(Erfurt)" title="Old Synagogue (Erfurt)">Old Synagogue</a> is still extant and a museum today, as is the <a href="/wiki/Mikveh" title="Mikveh">mikveh</a> at Gera river near <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Krämerbrücke</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-mikveh_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mikveh-12">[11]</a></sup> In 1349, during the wave of <a href="/wiki/Black_Death_Jewish_persecutions" title="Black Death Jewish persecutions">Black Death Jewish persecutions</a> across Europe, the Jews of Erfurt were rounded up, with <a href="/wiki/Erfurt_massacre_(1349)" title="Erfurt massacre (1349)">more than 100 killed</a> and the rest driven from the city. Before the persecution, a wealthy Jewish merchant buried his property in the basement of his house. In 1998, this treasure was found during construction works. The <a href="/wiki/Erfurt_Treasure" title="Erfurt Treasure">Erfurt Treasure</a> with various gold and silver objects is shown in the exhibition in the synagogue today.<sup id="cite_ref-AID_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AID-13">[12]</a></sup> Only a few years after 1349, the Jews moved back to Erfurt and founded a second community, which was disbanded by the city council in 1458.</p>
<p>In 1379,<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-14">[13]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Erfurt" title="University of Erfurt">University of Erfurt</a> was founded. Together with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cologne" title="University of Cologne">University of Cologne</a> it was one of the first city-owned universities in Germany, while they were usually owned by the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Territorial_lord" title="Territorial lord">Landesherren</a></span></i>. Some buildings of this old university are extant or restored in the "Latin Quarter" in the northern city centre (like <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">Collegium Maius</span>, student dorms "<span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Georgenburse</span>" and others, the hospital and the church of the university). The university quickly became a hotspot of German cultural life in <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_humanism" title="Renaissance humanism">Renaissance humanism</a> with scholars like <a href="/wiki/Ulrich_von_Hutten" title="Ulrich von Hutten">Ulrich von Hutten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Helius_Eobanus_Hessus" title="Helius Eobanus Hessus">Helius Eobanus Hessus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Justus_Jonas" title="Justus Jonas">Justus Jonas</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_period">Early modern period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early modern period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Erfurt-1650-Merian.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Erfurt-1650-Merian.jpg/220px-Erfurt-1650-Merian.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Erfurt-1650-Merian.jpg/330px-Erfurt-1650-Merian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Erfurt-1650-Merian.jpg/440px-Erfurt-1650-Merian.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3176" data-file-height="2355" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Erfurt-1650-Merian.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Erfurt in 1650</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luftbild_Statthalterei.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Luftbild_Statthalterei.jpg/220px-Luftbild_Statthalterei.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Luftbild_Statthalterei.jpg/330px-Luftbild_Statthalterei.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Luftbild_Statthalterei.jpg/440px-Luftbild_Statthalterei.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1158" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luftbild_Statthalterei.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurmainzische_Statthalterei" class="extiw" title="de:Kurmainzische Statthalterei">Kurmainzische Statthalterei</a></span></i>, seat of the governors of Erfurt (at front)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Erfurt_(German_States)_1645_10_Ducat_(Portugaloser).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Erfurt_%28German_States%29_1645_10_Ducat_%28Portugaloser%29.jpg/220px-Erfurt_%28German_States%29_1645_10_Ducat_%28Portugaloser%29.jpg" width="220" height="111" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Erfurt_%28German_States%29_1645_10_Ducat_%28Portugaloser%29.jpg/330px-Erfurt_%28German_States%29_1645_10_Ducat_%28Portugaloser%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Erfurt_%28German_States%29_1645_10_Ducat_%28Portugaloser%29.jpg/440px-Erfurt_%28German_States%29_1645_10_Ducat_%28Portugaloser%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5802" data-file-height="2929" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Erfurt_(German_States)_1645_10_Ducat_(Portugaloser).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Christina, Queen of Sweden, depicted on a 1645 Erfurt 10 ducat coin. <sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[note 2]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1501 <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> (1483 - 1546) moved to Erfurt and began his studies at the university, finishing in 1509 with a doctorate degree.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-14">[13]</a></sup> After 1505, he lived in the Augustinian Monastery. In 1507 he became a priest at Erfurt Cathedral. He moved to <a href="/wiki/Wittenberg" title="Wittenberg">Wittenberg</a> in 1511. His <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a> found its way to Erfurt in 1521.</p>
<p>In 1530, the city became one of the first in Europe to be officially bi-confessional with the <a href="/wiki/Hammelburg" title="Hammelburg">Hammelburg</a> Treaty. It kept that status through all the following centuries. The later 16th and the 17th century brought a slow economic decline of Erfurt. Trade shrank, the population was falling and the university lost its influence. The city's independence was endangered. In 1664, the city and surrounding area were brought under the dominion of the <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Mainz" title="Electorate of Mainz">Electorate of Mainz</a> and the city lost its independence. The Electorate built a huge fortress on Petersberg hill between 1665 and 1726 to control the city and instituted a governor to rule Erfurt.</p>
<p>During the late 18th century, Erfurt saw another cultural peak. Governor <a href="/wiki/Karl_Theodor_Anton_Maria_von_Dalberg" title="Karl Theodor Anton Maria von Dalberg">Karl Theodor Anton Maria von Dalberg</a> had close relations with <a href="/wiki/Johann_Wolfgang_von_Goethe" title="Johann Wolfgang von Goethe">Johann Wolfgang von Goethe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Schiller" title="Friedrich Schiller">Friedrich Schiller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Gottfried_Herder" title="Johann Gottfried Herder">Johann Gottfried Herder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christoph_Martin_Wieland" title="Christoph Martin Wieland">Christoph Martin Wieland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_von_Humboldt" title="Wilhelm von Humboldt">Wilhelm von Humboldt</a>, who often visited him at his court in Erfurt.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Erfurt_during_the_Napoleonic_Wars">Erfurt during the Napoleonic Wars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Erfurt during the Napoleonic Wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Erfurt" title="Principality of Erfurt">Principality of Erfurt</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Die_Napoleonsh%C3%B6he_im_Steiger_bei_Erfurt_von_NH_Dornheim.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Die_Napoleonsh%C3%B6he_im_Steiger_bei_Erfurt_von_NH_Dornheim.jpg/220px-Die_Napoleonsh%C3%B6he_im_Steiger_bei_Erfurt_von_NH_Dornheim.jpg" width="220" height="266" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Die_Napoleonsh%C3%B6he_im_Steiger_bei_Erfurt_von_NH_Dornheim.jpg/330px-Die_Napoleonsh%C3%B6he_im_Steiger_bei_Erfurt_von_NH_Dornheim.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b1/Die_Napoleonsh%C3%B6he_im_Steiger_bei_Erfurt_von_NH_Dornheim.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="483" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Die_Napoleonsh%C3%B6he_im_Steiger_bei_Erfurt_von_NH_Dornheim.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Die Napoleonshöhe im Steiger bei Erfurt</span></i>, painted by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nikolaus_Dornheim&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nikolaus Dornheim (page does not exist)">Nikolaus Dornheim</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikolaus_Christian_Heinrich_Dornheim" class="extiw" title="de:Nikolaus Christian Heinrich Dornheim">de</a>)</span> in 1812. Inaugurated in March 1811 to celebrate <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>'s birthday, this <a href="/wiki/Greek_Revival_architecture" title="Greek Revival architecture">Greek-style</a> <a href="/wiki/Temple" title="Temple">temple</a> with grotto, flowerbeds and fountain in the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Stiegerwald</span></i> was burned in November 1813 and completely destroyed by Erfurters and their <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Sixth_Coalition" title="War of the Sixth Coalition">besiegers</a> in 1814.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Erfurt became part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Kingdom of Prussia</a> in 1802, to compensate for territories Prussia lost to France on the <a href="/wiki/Left_Bank_of_the_Rhine" title="Left Bank of the Rhine">Left Bank of the Rhine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reichsdeputationshauptschluss_documentArchive.de_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reichsdeputationshauptschluss_documentArchive.de-19">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reichsdeputationshauptschluss_Wikisource_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reichsdeputationshauptschluss_Wikisource-20">[18]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Capitulation_of_Erfurt" title="Capitulation of Erfurt">Capitulation of Erfurt</a> the city, its 12,000 Prussian and Saxon defenders under <a href="/wiki/William_I_of_the_Netherlands" title="William I of the Netherlands">William VI, Prince of Orange-Nassau</a>, 65 artillery pieces, and the Petersberg and Cyriaksburg fortresses (<i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Zitadellen von <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zitadelle_Petersberg" class="extiw" title="de:Zitadelle Petersberg">Petersberg</a> und <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zitadelle_Cyriaksburg" class="extiw" title="de:Zitadelle Cyriaksburg">Cyriaksburg</a></span></i>) were handed over to the French on 16 October 1806;<sup id="cite_ref-Petre_1907.2F1993_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Petre_1907.2F1993-21">[19]</a></sup> At the time of the capitulation, <a href="/wiki/Joachim_Murat" title="Joachim Murat">Joachim Murat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshal_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Marshal of France">Marshal of France</a>, had about 16,000 troops near Erfurt.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith_1998_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith_1998-22">[20]</a></sup> With the attachment of the <a href="/wiki/Saxe-Weimar" title="Saxe-Weimar">Saxe-Weimar</a> territory of <a href="/wiki/Blankenhain" title="Blankenhain">Blankenhain</a>, the city became part of the <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">First French Empire</a> in 1806 as the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Erfurt" title="Principality of Erfurt">Principality of Erfurt</a>, directly subordinate to Napoleon as an "imperial state domain" (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr"><i>domaine réservé à l'empereur</i></span>), separate from the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_the_Rhine" title="Confederation of the Rhine">Confederation of the Rhine</a>, which the surrounding <a href="/wiki/Thuringia" title="Thuringia">Thuringian</a> states had joined.<sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814-23">[21]</a></sup> Erfurt was administered by a civilian and military Senate<sup id="cite_ref-F.C3.BCrstenkongress_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F.C3.BCrstenkongress-24">[22]</a></sup> (<i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Finanz- und Domänenkammer Erfurt</span></i>)<sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814-23">[21]</a></sup> under a French governor, based in the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurmainzische_Statthalterei" class="extiw" title="de:Kurmainzische Statthalterei">Kurmainzische Statthalterei</a></span>, previously the seat of city's governor under the Electorate.<sup id="cite_ref-F.C3.BCrstenkongress_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F.C3.BCrstenkongress-24">[22]</a></sup> Napoleon first visited the principality on 23 July 1807, inspecting the citadels and fortifications.<sup id="cite_ref-F.C3.BCrstenkongress_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F.C3.BCrstenkongress-24">[22]</a></sup> In 1808, the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Erfurt" title="Congress of Erfurt">Congress of Erfurt</a> was held with <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia" title="Alexander I of Russia">Alexander I of Russia</a> visiting the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814-23">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>During their administration, the French introduced <a href="/wiki/Street_light" title="Street light">street lighting</a> and a tax on foreign horses to pay for maintaining the <a href="/wiki/Road_surface" title="Road surface">road surface</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814-23">[21]</a></sup> The <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peterskirche_(Erfurt)" class="extiw" title="de:Peterskirche (Erfurt)">Peterskirche</a></span> suffered under the French occupation, with its inventory being auctioned off to other local churches — including the <a href="/wiki/Organ_(music)" title="Organ (music)">organ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Church_bell" title="Church bell">bells</a> and even the <a href="/wiki/Steeple" title="Steeple">tower</a> of the <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">Corpus Christi</span> chapel (<i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Fronleichnamskapelle</span></i>) — and the former monastery's library being donated to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Erfurt" title="University of Erfurt">University of Erfurt</a> (and then to the Boineburg Library when the university closed in 1816).<sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814-23">[21]</a></sup> Similarly the Cyriaksburg Citadel was damaged by the French, with the city-side walls being partially dismantled in the hunt for imagined treasures from the convent, workers being paid from the sale of the building materials.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1811, to commemorate the birth of the <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_II" title="Napoleon II">Prince Imperial</a>, a 70-foot (21-metre) ceremonial <a href="/wiki/Column" title="Column">column</a> (<i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Die Napoleonsäule</span></i>) of wood and plaster was erected on the <a href="/wiki/Common_land" title="Common land">common</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814-23">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Denkmale_Erfurts_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denkmale_Erfurts-26">[24]</a></sup> Similarly, the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Napoleonshöhe</span></i> — a <a href="/wiki/Greek_Revival_architecture" title="Greek Revival architecture">Greek-style</a> <a href="/wiki/Temple" title="Temple">temple</a> topped by a <a href="/wiki/Winged_Victory_of_Samothrace" title="Winged Victory of Samothrace">winged victory</a> with shield, sword and lance and containing a <a href="/wiki/Bust_(sculpture)" title="Bust (sculpture)">bust</a> of Napoleon sculpted by <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Wilhelm_Eugen_D%C3%B6ll" title="Friedrich Wilhelm Eugen Döll">Friedrich Döll</a><sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814-23">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Denkmale_Erfurts_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denkmale_Erfurts-26">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup> — was erected in the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Stiegerwald</span></i> woods, including a grotto with fountain and flower beds, using a large pond (<i><span lang="la" xml:lang="la">lavoratorium</span></i>) from the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Peterskirche</span>,<sup id="cite_ref-Denkmale_Erfurts_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denkmale_Erfurts-26">[24]</a></sup> inaugurated with ceremony on 14 August 1811 after extravagant celebrations for Napoleon's birthday,<sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814-23">[21]</a></sup> which were repeated in 1812 with a concert in the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Predigerkirche_(Erfurt)" title="Predigerkirche (Erfurt)">Predigerkirche</a></span> conducted by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Spohr" title="Louis Spohr">Louis Spohr</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814-23">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Sixth_Coalition" title="War of the Sixth Coalition">Sixth Coalition</a> forming after French defeat in Russia, on 24 February 1813 Napoleon ordered the Petersburg Citadel to prepare for <a href="/wiki/Siege" title="Siege">siege</a>, visiting the city on 25 April to inspect the fortifications, in particular both Citadels.<sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814-23">[21]</a></sup> On 10 July 1813, Napoleon put <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandre_d%27Alton&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alexandre d'Alton (page does not exist)">Alexandre d'Alton</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexandre_d%27Alton" class="extiw" title="fr:Alexandre d'Alton">fr</a>)</span>, <a href="/wiki/Nobility_of_the_First_French_Empire" title="Nobility of the First French Empire">baron of the Empire</a>, in charge of the defences of Erfurt. However, when the French decreed that 1000 men would be conscripted into the <span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr">Grande Armée</span>, the recruits were joined by other citizens in rioting on 19 July that led to 20 arrests, of whom 2 were <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment" title="Capital punishment">sentenced to death</a> by French <a href="/wiki/Court-martial" title="Court-martial">court-martial</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814-23">[21]</a></sup> as a result, the French ordered the closure of all inns and alehouses.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Within a week of the Sixth Coalition's decisive <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leipzig" title="Battle of Leipzig">victory at Leipzig</a> (16–19 October 1813), however, Erfurt was besieged by Prussian, Austrian and Russian troops under the command of Prussian Lt Gen <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Graf_Kleist_von_Nollendorf" title="Friedrich Graf Kleist von Nollendorf">von Kleist</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814-23">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Koch_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Koch-29">[27]</a></sup> After a first capitulation signed by d'Alton on 20 December 1813 the French troops withdrew to the two fortresses of Petersberg and Cyriaksburg,<sup id="cite_ref-Koch_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Koch-29">[27]</a></sup> allowing for the Coalition forces to march into Erfurt on 6 January 1814 to jubilant greetings;<sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1814.E2.80.931850_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1814.E2.80.931850-30">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-H.C3.BChn_1839_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H.C3.BChn_1839-31">[29]</a></sup> the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Napoleonsäule</span></i> ceremonial column was burned and destroyed as a symbol of the citizens' oppression under the French;<sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814-23">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Denkmale_Erfurts_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denkmale_Erfurts-26">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1814.E2.80.931850_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1814.E2.80.931850-30">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup> similarly the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Napoleonshöhe</span></i> was burned on 1 November 1813 and completely destroyed by Erfurters and their besiegers in 1814.<sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814-23">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Denkmale_Erfurts_26-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denkmale_Erfurts-26">[24]</a></sup> After a call for volunteers 3 days later, 300 Erfurters joined the Coalition armies in France.<sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1814.E2.80.931850_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1814.E2.80.931850-30">[28]</a></sup> Finally, in May 1814, the French capitulated fully, with 1,700 French troops vacating the Petersberg and Cyriaksburg fortresses.<sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1814.E2.80.931850_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1814.E2.80.931850-30">[28]</a></sup> During the two and a half months of siege, the mortality rate rose in the city greatly; 1,564 Erfurt citizens died in 1813, around a thousand more than the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-H.C3.BChn_1839_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H.C3.BChn_1839-31">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a>, Erfurt was restored to <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Prussia</a> on 21 June 1815, becoming the capital of one of the three districts (<i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Regierungsbezirke</span></i>) of the new <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Saxony" title="Province of Saxony">Province of Saxony</a>, but some southern and eastern parts of Erfurter lands joined Blankenhain in being transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Saxe-Weimar-Eisenach" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Duchy of Saxe-Weimar-Eisenach">Grand Duchy of Saxe-Weimar-Eisenach</a> the following September.<sup id="cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1814.E2.80.931850_30-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1814.E2.80.931850-30">[28]</a></sup> Although enclosed by <a href="/wiki/Thuringia" title="Thuringia">Thuringian</a> territory in the west, south and east, the city remained part of the Prussian <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Saxony" title="Province of Saxony">Province of Saxony</a> until 1944.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Since_1815">Since 1815</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Since 1815">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kaffeetrichter2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Kaffeetrichter2.JPG/220px-Kaffeetrichter2.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Kaffeetrichter2.JPG/330px-Kaffeetrichter2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Kaffeetrichter2.JPG/440px-Kaffeetrichter2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kieler_Stra%C3%9Fe_Erfurt.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Kieler_Stra%C3%9Fe_Erfurt.JPG/220px-Kieler_Stra%C3%9Fe_Erfurt.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Kieler_Stra%C3%9Fe_Erfurt.JPG/330px-Kieler_Stra%C3%9Fe_Erfurt.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Kieler_Stra%C3%9Fe_Erfurt.JPG/440px-Kieler_Stra%C3%9Fe_Erfurt.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

Housing projects in <a href="/wiki/Bauhaus" title="Bauhaus">Bauhaus</a> style from 1930</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J0422-0203-002,_Erfurt,_Hotel_%22Erfurter_Hof%22.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J0422-0203-002%2C_Erfurt%2C_Hotel_%22Erfurter_Hof%22.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J0422-0203-002%2C_Erfurt%2C_Hotel_%22Erfurter_Hof%22.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J0422-0203-002%2C_Erfurt%2C_Hotel_%22Erfurter_Hof%22.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J0422-0203-002%2C_Erfurt%2C_Hotel_%22Erfurter_Hof%22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J0422-0203-002%2C_Erfurt%2C_Hotel_%22Erfurter_Hof%22.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J0422-0203-002%2C_Erfurt%2C_Hotel_%22Erfurter_Hof%22.jpg 2x" data-file-width="764" data-file-height="515" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J0422-0203-002,_Erfurt,_Hotel_%22Erfurter_Hof%22.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hotel "<span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Erfurter Hof</span>", place of the first meeting of <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West</a> German heads of government in 1970</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848_in_the_German_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Revolutions of 1848 in the German states">1848 Revolution</a>, many Germans desired to have a united national state. An attempt in this direction was the failed <a href="/wiki/Erfurt_Union" title="Erfurt Union">Erfurt Union</a> of German states in 1850.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> reached Erfurt in the 1840s, when the <a href="/wiki/Thuringian_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Thuringian Railway">Thuringian Railway</a> connecting <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> was built. During the following years, many factories in different sectors were founded. One of the biggest was the "Royal Gun Factory of <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>" in 1862. After German Unification in 1871, Erfurt moved from the southern border of Prussia to the centre of Germany, so that the fortifications of the city were not needed anymore. The demolition of the city fortifications in 1873 led to a construction boom in Erfurt, because it was now possible to build in the area formerly occupied by the city walls and beyond. Many public and private buildings emerged and the infrastructure (such as tramway, hospitals, schools) improved rapidly. The number of inhabitants grew from 40,000 around 1870 to 130,000 in 1914 and the city expanded in all directions.</p>
<p>The "<a href="/wiki/Erfurt_Program" title="Erfurt Program">Erfurt Program</a>" was adopted by the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democratic Party of Germany</a> during its congress at Erfurt in 1891.</p>
<p>Between the wars, the city kept growing. Housing shortages were fought with building programmes and social infrastructure was broadened according to the welfare policy in the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">Weimar Republic</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> between 1929 and 1932 led to a disaster for Erfurt, nearly one out of three became unemployed. Conflicts between far-left and far-right oriented milieus increased and many inhabitants supported the new Nazi government and <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>. Others, especially some communist workers, put up resistance against the new administration. In 1938, the new synagogue was destroyed during the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Kristallnacht" title="Kristallnacht">Kristallnacht</a></span>. Jews lost their property and emigrated or were deported to <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps" title="Nazi concentration camps">Nazi concentration camps</a> (together with many communists). In 1914, the company <i><a href="/wiki/Topf_and_Sons" title="Topf and Sons">Topf and Sons</a></i> began the manufacture of crematoria later becoming the market leader in this industry. Under the Nazis, <i>JA Topf &amp; Sons</i> supplied specially developed crematoria, ovens and associated plant to the <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz-Birkenau" class="mw-redirect" title="Auschwitz-Birkenau">Auschwitz-Birkenau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buchenwald" class="mw-redirect" title="Buchenwald">Buchenwald</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mauthausen-Gusen" class="mw-redirect" title="Mauthausen-Gusen">Mauthausen-Gusen</a> concentration camps. On 27 January 2011 a memorial and museum dedicated to the Holocaust victims was opened at the former company premises in Erfurt.</p>
<p>Bombed as a target of the <a href="/wiki/Oil_Campaign_of_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil Campaign of World War II">Oil Campaign of World War II</a>, Erfurt suffered only limited damage and was captured on 12 April 1945, by the US <a href="/wiki/80th_Infantry_Division_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="80th Infantry Division (United States)">80th Infantry Division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> On 3 July, American troops left the city, which then became part of the <a href="/wiki/Allied_Occupation_Zones_in_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Allied Occupation Zones in Germany">Soviet Zone of Occupation</a> and eventually of the German Democratic Republic (<a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a>). In 1948, Erfurt became the capital of <a href="/wiki/Thuringia" title="Thuringia">Thuringia</a>, replacing <a href="/wiki/Weimar" title="Weimar">Weimar</a>. In 1952, the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">Länder</a></span> in the GDR were dissolved in favour of centralization under the new socialist government. Erfurt then became the capital of a new "<span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Erfurt_(Bezirk)" class="mw-redirect" title="Erfurt (Bezirk)">Bezirk</a></span>" (district). In 1953, the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Hochschule" title="Hochschule">Hochschule</a></span> of education was founded, followed by the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Hochschule</span> of medicine in 1954, the first academical institutions in Erfurt since the closing of the university in 1816.</p>
<p>On 19 March 1970, the East and West German heads of government <a href="/wiki/Willi_Stoph" title="Willi Stoph">Willi Stoph</a> and <a href="/wiki/Willy_Brandt" title="Willy Brandt">Willy Brandt</a> met in Erfurt, the first such meeting since the division of Germany. During the 1970s and 1980s, as the economic situation in GDR worsened, many old buildings in city centre decayed, while the government fought against the housing shortage by building large <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Plattenbau" title="Plattenbau">Plattenbau</a></span> settlements in the periphery. The <a href="/wiki/Peaceful_Revolution" title="Peaceful Revolution">Peaceful Revolution</a> of 1989/1990 led to <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DDR_Street_signs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/DDR_Street_signs.jpg/220px-DDR_Street_signs.jpg" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/DDR_Street_signs.jpg/330px-DDR_Street_signs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/DDR_Street_signs.jpg/440px-DDR_Street_signs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1688" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DDR_Street_signs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Socialist-era street signs removed from around the city of Erfurt after 1990</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With the re-formation of the state of <a href="/wiki/Thuringia" title="Thuringia">Thuringia</a> in 1990, the city became the state capital. After reunification, a deep economic crisis occurred in Eastern Germany. Many factories closed and many people lost their jobs and moved to the former West Germany. At the same time, many buildings were redeveloped and the infrastructure improved massively. In 1994, the new university was opened, as was the Fachhochschule in 1991. Between 2005 and 2008, the economic situation improved as the unemployment rate decreased and new enterprises developed. In addition, the population began to increase once again.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_demographics">Geography and demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography and demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Erfurt.Gera_Fluss.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Erfurt.Gera_Fluss.jpg/220px-Erfurt.Gera_Fluss.jpg" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Erfurt.Gera_Fluss.jpg/330px-Erfurt.Gera_Fluss.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Erfurt.Gera_Fluss.jpg/440px-Erfurt.Gera_Fluss.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5720" data-file-height="3479" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Erfurt.Gera_Fluss.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gera river in the city centre</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">Topography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Topography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Erfurt is situated in the south of the <a href="/wiki/Thuringian_basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Thuringian basin">Thuringian basin</a>, a fertile agricultural area between the <a href="/wiki/Harz" title="Harz">Harz</a> mountains 80&#160;km (50&#160;mi) to the north and the <a href="/wiki/Thuringian_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Thuringian forest">Thuringian forest</a> 30&#160;km (19&#160;mi) to the southwest. Whereas the northern parts of the city area are flat, the southern ones consist of hilly landscape up to 430 m of elevation. In this part lies the municipal forest of <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Steigerwald</span></i> with <a href="/wiki/Fagus_sylvatica" title="Fagus sylvatica">beeches</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quercus_robur" title="Quercus robur">oaks</a> as main tree species. To the east and to the west are some non-forested hills so that the <a href="/wiki/Gera_(river)" title="Gera (river)">Gera</a> river valley within the town forms a basin. North of the city are some <a href="/wiki/Gravel_pit" title="Gravel pit">gravel pits</a> in operation, while others are abandoned, flooded and used as leisure areas.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Erfurt has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (Dfb) or an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (<i>Cfb</i>) according to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-koppen_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-koppen-34">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Peel_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel-35">[33]</a></sup> Summers are warm and sometimes humid with average high temperatures of 23&#160;°C (73&#160;°F) and lows of 12&#160;°C (54&#160;°F). Winters are relatively cold with average high temperatures of 2&#160;°C (36&#160;°F) and lows of −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F). The city's topography creates a microclimate caused by the location inside a basin with sometimes <a href="/wiki/Inversion_(meteorology)" title="Inversion (meteorology)">inversion</a> in winter (quite cold nights under −20&#160;°C (−4&#160;°F)) and inadequate air circulation in summer. Annual precipitation is only 502 millimeters (19.8&#160;in) with moderate rainfall throughout the year. Light snowfall mainly occurs from December through February, but snow cover does not usually remain for long.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_division">Administrative division</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Administrative division">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Erfurt-Ortsteile.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Erfurt-Ortsteile.png/220px-Erfurt-Ortsteile.png" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Erfurt-Ortsteile.png/330px-Erfurt-Ortsteile.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Erfurt-Ortsteile.png/440px-Erfurt-Ortsteile.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Erfurt-Ortsteile.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Districts of Erfurt</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Erfurt abuts the districts of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6mmerda_(district)" title="Sömmerda (district)">Sömmerda</a> (municipalities <a href="/wiki/Witterda" title="Witterda">Witterda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elxleben" title="Elxleben">Elxleben</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walschleben" title="Walschleben">Walschleben</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riethnordhausen,_Thuringia" title="Riethnordhausen, Thuringia">Riethnordhausen</a>, <a href="/wiki/N%C3%B6da" title="Nöda">Nöda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alperstedt" title="Alperstedt">Alperstedt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9Frudestedt" title="Großrudestedt">Großrudestedt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Udestedt" title="Udestedt">Udestedt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kleinm%C3%B6lsen" title="Kleinmölsen">Kleinmölsen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9Fm%C3%B6lsen" title="Großmölsen">Großmölsen</a>) in the north, <a href="/wiki/Weimarer_Land" title="Weimarer Land">Weimarer Land</a> (municipalities <a href="/wiki/Niederzimmern" title="Niederzimmern">Niederzimmern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nohra" title="Nohra">Nohra</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6nchenholzhausen" title="Mönchenholzhausen">Mönchenholzhausen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Klettbach" title="Klettbach">Klettbach</a>) in the east, <a href="/wiki/Ilm-Kreis" title="Ilm-Kreis">Ilm-Kreis</a> (municipalities <a href="/wiki/Kirchheim,_Thuringia" title="Kirchheim, Thuringia">Kirchheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rockhausen" title="Rockhausen">Rockhausen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amt_Wachsenburg" title="Amt Wachsenburg">Amt Wachsenburg</a>) in the south and <a href="/wiki/Gotha_(district)" title="Gotha (district)">Gotha</a> (municipalities <a href="/wiki/Nesse-Apfelst%C3%A4dt" title="Nesse-Apfelstädt">Nesse-Apfelstädt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nottleben" title="Nottleben">Nottleben</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zimmernsupra" title="Zimmernsupra">Zimmernsupra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bienst%C3%A4dt" title="Bienstädt">Bienstädt</a>) in the west.</p>
<p>The city itself is divided into 53 districts. The centre is formed by the district <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Altstadt</span></i> (old town) and the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCnderzeit" title="Gründerzeit">Gründerzeit</a></span> districts <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Andreasvorstadt</span></i> in the northwest, <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Johannesvorstadt</span></i> in the northeast, <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Krämpfervorstadt</span></i> in the east, <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Daberstedt</span></i> in the southeast, <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Löbervorstadt</span></i> in the southwest and <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Brühlervorstadt</span></i> in the west. More former industrial districts are <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Ilversgehofen</span></i> (incorporated in 1911), <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Hohenwinden</span></i> and <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Sulzer Siedlung</span></i> in the north. Another group of districts is marked by <a href="/wiki/Plattenbau" title="Plattenbau">Plattenbau</a> settlements, constructed during the <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">GDR</a> period: <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Berliner Platz</span></i>, <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Moskauer Platz</span></i>, <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Rieth</span></i>, <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Roter Berg</span></i> and <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Johannesplatz</span></i> in the northern as well as <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Melchendorf</span></i>, <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Wiesenhügel</span></i> and <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Herrenberg</span></i> in the southern city parts.</p>
<p>Finally, there are many villages with an average population of approximately 1,000 which were incorporated during the 20th century; however, they mostly stayed rural to date:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-3" style="-moz-column-count: 3; -webkit-column-count: 3; column-count: 3;">

</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Around the year 1500, the city had 18,000 inhabitants and was one of the largest cities in the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>. The population then more or less stagnated until the 19th century. The population of Erfurt was 21,000 in 1820, and increased to 32,000 in 1847, the year of rail connection as industrialization began. In the following decades Erfurt grew up to 130,000 at the beginning of World War I and 190,000 inhabitants in 1950. A maximum was reached in 1988 with 220,000 persons. The bad economic situation in eastern Germany after the reunification resulted in a decline in population, which fell to 200,000 in 2002 before rising again to 206,000 in 2011. The average growth of population between 2009 and 2012 was approximately 0.68% p. a, whereas the population in bordering rural regions is shrinking with accelerating tendency. Suburbanization played only a small role in Erfurt. It occurred after reunification for a short time in the 1990s, but most of the suburban areas were situated within the administrative city borders.</p>
<p>The birth deficit was 200 in 2012, this is -1.0 per 1,000 inhabitants (Thuringian average: -4.5; national average: -2.4). The net migration rate was +8.3 per 1,000 inhabitants in 2012 (Thuringian average: -0.8; national average: +4.6).<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> The most important regions of origin of Erfurt migrants are rural areas of Thuringia, <a href="/wiki/Saxony-Anhalt" title="Saxony-Anhalt">Saxony-Anhalt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saxony" title="Saxony">Saxony</a> as well as foreign countries like Poland, Russia, Ukraine, Hungary, Serbia, Romania and Bulgaria.</p>
<p>Like other eastern German cities, foreigners account only for a small share of Erfurt's population: circa 3.0% are non-Germans by citizenship and overall 5.9% are migrants (according to the <a href="/wiki/2011_EU_census" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 EU census">2011 EU census</a>). Differing from the national average, the most important groups of migrants in Erfurt are <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_people_in_Germany" title="Vietnamese people in Germany">Vietnamese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_Germany" title="Russians in Germany">Russians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians_in_Germany" title="Ukrainians in Germany">Ukrainians</a>.</p>
<p>Due to the official atheism of the former <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">GDR</a>, most of the population is non-religious. 14.8% are members of the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Church_in_Central_Germany" title="Evangelical Church in Central Germany">Evangelical Church in Central Germany</a> and 6.8% are Catholics (according to the 2011 EU census). The Jewish Community consists of 500 members. Most of them migrated to Erfurt from Russia and Ukraine in the 1990s.</p>
<h2><span id="Culture,_sights_and_cityscape"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture.2C_sights_and_cityscape">Culture, sights and cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Culture, sights and cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Residents_notable_in_cultural_history">Residents notable in cultural history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Residents notable in cultural history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Erfurt" title="List of people from Erfurt">List of people from Erfurt</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> (1483-1546) studied law and philosophy at the University of Erfurt from 1501. He gained his B.A. (1502) and M.A. (1505).<sup id="cite_ref-uni-erfurt.de_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uni-erfurt.de-4">[4]</a></sup> He lived in <a href="/wiki/St._Augustine%27s_Monastery_(Erfurt)" title="St. Augustine's Monastery (Erfurt)">St. Augustine's Monastery</a> in Erfurt, as a monk from 1505 to 1511.<sup id="cite_ref-augustinerkloster.de_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-augustinerkloster.de-38">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>The theologian, philosopher and mystic <a href="/wiki/Meister_Eckhart" title="Meister Eckhart">Meister Eckhart</a> (c. 1260-1328) entered the Dominican monastery in Erfurt when he was aged about 18 (around 1275). Eckhart was the Dominican Prior at Erfurt from 1294 until 1298, and Vicar of Thuringia from 1298 to 1302. After a year in Paris, he returned to Erfurt in 1303 and administered his duties as Provincial of Saxony from there until 1311.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Max_Weber" title="Max Weber">Max Weber</a> (1864 - 1920) was born in Erfurt.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup> He was a sociologist, philosopher, jurist, and political economist whose ideas have profoundly influenced modern social theory and social research.</p>
<p>The textile designer <a href="/wiki/Margaretha_Reichardt" title="Margaretha Reichardt">Margaretha Reichardt</a> (1907 - 1984) was born and died in Erfurt. She studied at the <a href="/wiki/Bauhaus" title="Bauhaus">Bauhaus</a> from 1926 to 1930,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup> and while there worked with <a href="/wiki/Marcel_Breuer" title="Marcel Breuer">Marcel Breuer</a> on his innovative chair designs. Her former home and weaving workshop in Erfurt, the <i>Margaretha Reichardt Haus</i>, is now a museum, managed by the Angermuseum Erfurt.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Johann_Pachelbel" title="Johann Pachelbel">Johann Pachelbel</a> (1653 - 1706) served as organist at the Prediger church in Erfurt from June 1678 until August 1690. Pachelbel composed approximately seventy pieces for organ while in Erfurt.</p>
<p>After 1906 the composer <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wetz" title="Richard Wetz">Richard Wetz</a> (1875 - 1935) lived in Erfurt and became the leading person in the town's musical life. His major works were written here, including three symphonies, a Requiem and a Christmas Oratorio.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Alexander_M%C3%BCller_(composer)" title="Alexander Müller (composer)">Alexander Müller</a> (1808 - 1863) pianist, conductor and composer, was born in Erfurt. He later moved to <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a>, where he served as leader of the General Music Society's subscription concerts series.</p>
<p>The city is the birthplace of one of <a href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Johann Sebastian Bach">Johann Sebastian Bach</a>'s cousins, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Bernhard_Bach" title="Johann Bernhard Bach">Johann Bernhard Bach</a>, as well as Johann Sebastian Bach's father <a href="/wiki/Johann_Ambrosius_Bach" title="Johann Ambrosius Bach">Johann Ambrosius Bach</a>. Bach's parents were married in 1668 in a small church, the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Kaufmannskirche</span></i> (Merchant's Church), that still exists on the main square, Anger.</p>
<p>Famous modern musicians from Erfurt are <a href="/wiki/Clueso" title="Clueso">Clueso</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Boogie_Pimps" title="Boogie Pimps">Boogie Pimps</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yvonne_Catterfeld" title="Yvonne Catterfeld">Yvonne Catterfeld</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Erfurt has a great variety of museums:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Stadtmuseum</span></i> (municipal museum) shows aspects of Erfurt's history with a focus on the Middle Ages, early modern history, Martin Luther and the university. Other parts of the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Stadtmuseum</span> are the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Neue Mühle</span></i> (new mill), an old water mill still in operation, and the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Benaryspeicher</span></i> (Benary's magazine) with an exhibition of old printing machines.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Alte Synagoge</span></i> (<a href="/wiki/Old_Synagogue_(Erfurt)" title="Old Synagogue (Erfurt)">Old Synagogue</a>) is the oldest Synagogue in Europe which is intact to its roof.<sup id="cite_ref-altsyn_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-altsyn-42">[40]</a></sup> Its museum was opened in 2009 and has exhibitions on the history of Erfurt's Jewish Community. It houses facsimiles of medieval Hebrew manuscripts and the <a href="/wiki/Erfurt_Treasure" title="Erfurt Treasure">Erfurt Treasure</a>, a hoard of coins, goldsmiths' work and jewellery that is assumed to have belonged to Jews who hid them in 1349 at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Erfurt_massacre_(1349)" title="Erfurt massacre (1349)">Black Death pogroms</a>.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Erinnerungsort Topf &amp; Söhne</span></i> (memorial site of <a href="/wiki/Topf_and_Sons" title="Topf and Sons">Topf and Sons</a>), on the site of the factory of the company which constructed crematoria for <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz" class="mw-redirect" title="Auschwitz">Auschwitz</a> and other concentration camps. It has exhibitions about the operations of the company and the holocaust.</li>
<li><i>Gedenk- und Bildungsstätte Andreasstraße Erfurt</i>, (Stasi Museum). On the site of the former Erfurt Stasi headquarters and prison, where over 5000 people were held. On 4 December 1989, the building was occupied by local residents. It was the first of many such takeovers of Stasi buildings in the former East Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> Today it has exhibitions on the history of East Germany and the activities of its regime.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Angermuseum</span></i> is one of the main art museums of Erfurt, named after Anger Square, where it is located. It focuses on modern graphic arts, medieval sculpture and early modern artisanal handicraft.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Kunsthalle Erfurt</span></i> (Erfurt City Art Gallery) has exhibitions of contemporary art, of local, national and international artists.</li>
<li>The <i>Margaretha Reichardt Haus</i> is the home and workshop of the textile designer and former Bauhaus student, <a href="/wiki/Margaretha_Reichardt" title="Margaretha Reichardt">Margaretha Reichardt</a> (1907 - 1984).<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Peterskirche</span></i> (Saint Peter's church) houses an exhibition of <a href="/wiki/Concrete_art" title="Concrete art">concrete art</a>, i.e. totally abstract art (not art made out of concrete).</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Deutsches Gartenbaumuseum</span></i> (National Museum of Horticulture) is housed in the 17th-century <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cyriaksburg_Citadel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cyriaksburg Citadel (page does not exist)">Cyriaksburg Citadel</a><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup> and shows the history of German horticulture, which has long been prominent in Erfurt.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Naturkundemuseum_Erfurt" title="Naturkundemuseum Erfurt">Naturkundemuseum</a></span></i> (Natural History Museum) is situated in a medieval woad warehouse and exhibits objects of Thuringian flora and fauna, geology and ecology.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Museum für Thüringer Volkskunde</span></i> (Museum of Folk Art and Cultural Anthropology) looks at the ordinary life of people in Thuringia in the past and shows exhibits of peasant and artisan traditions.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Elektromuseum</span></i> (Museum of Electrical Engineering) shows the history of electric engines, which have featured prominently in Erfurt's economy.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Schloss_Molsdorf&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Schloss Molsdorf (page does not exist)">Schloss Molsdorf</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schloss_Molsdorf" class="extiw" title="de:Schloss Molsdorf">de</a>)</span> in the district of Molsdorf is a <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque</a> palace with an exhibition about the painter <a href="/w/index.php?title=Otto_Kn%C3%B6pfer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Otto Knöpfer (page does not exist)">Otto Knöpfer</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Otto_Kn%C3%B6pfer" class="extiw" title="de:Otto Knöpfer">de</a>)</span>.</li>
</ul>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
