<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre">Theatre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Theatre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since 2003, the modern opera house is home to <a href="/wiki/Theater_Erfurt" title="Theater Erfurt">Theater Erfurt</a> and its Philharmonic Orchestra. The "grand stage" section has 800 seats and the "studio stage" can hold 200 spectators. In September 2005, the opera <i><a href="/wiki/Waiting_for_the_Barbarians_(opera)" title="Waiting for the Barbarians (opera)">Waiting for the Barbarians</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Philip_Glass" title="Philip Glass">Philip Glass</a> premiered in the opera house. The Erfurt Theater has been a source of controversy recently. In 2005, a performance of <a href="/wiki/Engelbert_Humperdinck_(composer)" title="Engelbert Humperdinck (composer)">Engelbert Humperdinck</a>'s opera <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/H%C3%A4nsel_und_Gretel_(opera)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hänsel und Gretel (opera)">Hänsel und Gretel</a></span></i> stirred up the local press since the performance contained suggestions of pedophilia and incest. The opera was advertised in the program with the addition "for adults only".</p>
<p>On 12 April 2008, a version of <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Verdi" title="Giuseppe Verdi">Verdi</a>'s opera <i><span lang="it" xml:lang="it"><a href="/wiki/Un_ballo_in_maschera" title="Un ballo in maschera">Un ballo in maschera</a></span></i> directed by Johann Kresnik opened at the Erfurt Theater. The production stirred deep controversy by featuring nude performers in <a href="/wiki/Mickey_Mouse" title="Mickey Mouse">Mickey Mouse</a> masks dancing on the ruins of the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_(1973-2001)" class="mw-redirect" title="World Trade Center (1973-2001)">World Trade Center</a> and a female singer with a painted on <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Hitler</a> toothbrush moustache performing a straight arm <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazi</a> salute, along with sinister portrayals of American soldiers, <a href="/wiki/Uncle_Sam" title="Uncle Sam">Uncle Sam</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a> impersonators. The director described the production as a populist critique of modern American society, aimed at showing up the disparities between rich and poor. The controversy prompted one local politician to call for locals to boycott the performances, but this was largely ignored and the première was sold out.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luftbild_Gunda_Niemann_Stirnemann_Halle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Luftbild_Gunda_Niemann_Stirnemann_Halle.jpg/220px-Luftbild_Gunda_Niemann_Stirnemann_Halle.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Luftbild_Gunda_Niemann_Stirnemann_Halle.jpg/330px-Luftbild_Gunda_Niemann_Stirnemann_Halle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Luftbild_Gunda_Niemann_Stirnemann_Halle.jpg/440px-Luftbild_Gunda_Niemann_Stirnemann_Halle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1158" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luftbild_Gunda_Niemann_Stirnemann_Halle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Gunda Niemann-Stirnemann Halle</span></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Messe_Erfurt" title="Messe Erfurt">Messe Erfurt</a> serves as playground for the <a href="/wiki/Oettinger_Rockets" title="Oettinger Rockets">Oettinger Rockets</a>, a professional basketball team in Germany's first division, the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_Bundesliga" title="Basketball Bundesliga">Basketball Bundesliga</a>.</p>
<p>Notable types of sport in Erfurt are athletics, ice skating, cycling (with the oldest velodrome in use in the world, opened in 1885), swimming, handball, volleyball, tennis and football. The city's football club <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/FC_Rot-Wei%C3%9F_Erfurt" title="FC Rot-Weiß Erfurt">FC Rot-Weiß Erfurt</a></span> is member of <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/3._Fu%C3%9Fball-Liga" class="mw-redirect" title="3. Fußball-Liga">3. Fußball-Liga</a></span> and based in <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Steigerwaldstadion" title="Steigerwaldstadion">Steigerwaldstadion</a></span> with a capacity of 20,000. The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Gunda Niemann-Stirnemann Halle</span></i> was the second <a href="/wiki/Speed_skating_rink#Indoor_speed_skating_tracks" title="Speed skating rink">indoor speed skating arena</a> in Germany.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Br%C3%BChlervorstadt.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Br%C3%BChlervorstadt.JPG/220px-Br%C3%BChlervorstadt.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Br%C3%BChlervorstadt.JPG/330px-Br%C3%BChlervorstadt.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Br%C3%BChlervorstadt.JPG/440px-Br%C3%BChlervorstadt.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Br%C3%BChlervorstadt.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Architecture from the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCnderzeit" title="Gründerzeit">Gründerzeit</a></span></i> in Brühlervorstadt district</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Erfurt's cityscape features a medieval core of narrow, curved alleys in the centre surrounded by a belt of <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCnderzeit" title="Gründerzeit">Gründerzeit</a></span></i> architecture, created between 1873 and 1914. In 1873, the city's fortifications were demolished and it became possible to build houses in the area in front of the former city walls. In the following years, Erfurt saw a construction boom. In the northern area (districts Andreasvorstadt, Johannesvorstadt and Ilversgehofen) <a href="/wiki/Tenement" title="Tenement">tenements</a> for the factory workers were built whilst the eastern area (Krämpfervorstadt and Daberstedt) featured apartments for white-collar workers and clerks and the southwestern part (Löbervorstadt and Brühlervorstadt) with its beautiful valley landscape saw the construction of villas and mansions of rich factory owners and notables.</p>
<p>During the interwar period, some settlements in <a href="/wiki/Bauhaus" title="Bauhaus">Bauhaus</a> style were realized, often as housing cooperatives.</p>
<p>After World War II and over the whole GDR period, housing shortages remained a problem even though the government started a big apartment construction programme. Between 1970 and 1990 large <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Plattenbau" title="Plattenbau">Plattenbau</a></span> settlements with high-rise blocks on the northern (for 50,000 inhabitants) and southeastern (for 40,000 inhabitants) periphery were constructed. After reunification the renovation of old houses in city centre and the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Gründerzeit</span></i> areas was a big issue. The federal government granted substantial subsidies, so that many houses could be restored.</p>
<p>Compared to many other German cities, little of Erfurt was destroyed in World War II. This is one reason why the centre today offers a mixture of medieval, Baroque and <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">Neoclassical architecture</a> as well as buildings from the last 150 years.</p>
<p>Public green spaces are located along Gera river and in several parks like the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Stadtpark</span></i>, the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Nordpark</span></i> and the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Südpark</span></i>. The largest green area is the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Egapark&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Egapark (page does not exist)">Egapark</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egapark" class="extiw" title="de:Egapark">de</a>)</span>, a horticultural exhibition park and botanic garden established in 1961.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sights_and_architectural_heritage">Sights and architectural heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sights and architectural heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="Churches,_monasteries_and_synagogues"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Churches.2C_monasteries_and_synagogues">Churches, monasteries and synagogues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Churches, monasteries and synagogues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Erfurter_Dom_von_Oben_08.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Erfurter_Dom_von_Oben_08.jpg/330px-Erfurter_Dom_von_Oben_08.jpg" width="330" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Erfurter_Dom_von_Oben_08.jpg/495px-Erfurter_Dom_von_Oben_08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Erfurter_Dom_von_Oben_08.jpg/660px-Erfurter_Dom_von_Oben_08.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4384" data-file-height="3288" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Erfurter_Dom_von_Oben_08.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
St Mary's Cathedral (left) and St Severus' Church (right) on Domberg hill</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city centre has about 25 churches and monasteries, most of them in <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> style, some also in <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> style or a mixture of Romanesque and Gothic elements, and a few in later styles. The various steeples characterize the medieval centre and led to one of Erfurt's nicknames as the "Thuringian Rome".<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Catholic_churches_and_monasteries">Catholic churches and monasteries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Catholic churches and monasteries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<ul>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Allerheiligenkirche</span></i> (All Saints' Church) is a 14th-century Gothic parish church in Market Street, which hosts a <a href="/wiki/Columbarium" title="Columbarium">columbarium</a>.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Dom St. Marien</span></i> (<a href="/wiki/Erfurt_Cathedral" title="Erfurt Cathedral">St Mary's Cathedral</a>) perches above Domplatz, the Catherdral square. It is the <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_see" title="Episcopal see">Episcopal see</a> and one of the main sights of Erfurt. It combines Romanesque and Gothic elements and has the largest medieval bell in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> which is named <a href="/wiki/Maria_Gloriosa" title="Maria Gloriosa">Gloriosa</a>. One of the works of art inside the Cathedral is <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Cranach_the_Elder" title="Lucas Cranach the Elder">Lucas Cranach the Elder's</a> 'The Mystic Marriage of St. Catherine' painted around 1520.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Lorenzkirche</span></i> (St Laurence's Church) is a small 14th-century Gothic parish church at Anger Square.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Martinikirche</span></i> (St Martin's Church) was built in the 15th century in Gothic style and later converted to Baroque style. It was both a <a href="/wiki/Cistercians" title="Cistercians">Cistercian</a> monastery and a parish church of Brühl, a medieval suburban zone.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Neuwerkskirche St. Crucis</span></i> (church of the new work/Holy Cross Church) is a 15th-century Gothic parish church at Neuwerk Street, that was later converted to Baroque style. Until 1285, it was used as an <a href="/wiki/Augustinians" title="Augustinians">Augustinian</a> monastery.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Schottenkirche St. Nikolai und St. Jakobi</span></i> (Scots Monks' Church of St Nicholas and St James) is an 11th-century Romanesque monastery church with a Baroque façade, which was later used as a parish church.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Severikirche</span></i> (St Severus' Church) is the second-largest parish church after the cathedral and stands next to it on the Domberg hill. It is a Gothic church and was built around 1300.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Ursulinenkirche</span></i>, St. Ursula's Church, is a Gothic church at Anger Square. It is attached to the Ursulinenkloster, St. Ursula's Nunnery, founded in 1136.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> It is the only medieval monastery or nunnery in Erfurt which has been in continuous operation since it opened.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Wigbertikirche</span></i> (St Wigbert's Church) is a 15th-century Gothic parish church at Anger Square.</li>
</ul>

<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Protestant_churches_and_monasteries">Protestant churches and monasteries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Protestant churches and monasteries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<ul>
<li><i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Ägidienkirche</span></i> (St Giles' Church) is a 14th-century Gothic parish church at <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Wenigenmarkt</span> Square. It is the surviving one of formerly two bridge-head churches of the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Kr%C3%A4merbr%C3%BCcke" title="Krämerbrücke">Krämerbrücke</a></span> located on both ends of the bridge. As a result, the nave is on the 1st floor, while on ground level is a passage to the bridge. The steeple is open to the public and offers a good view over the city centre. Today, St Giles' Church is a <a href="/wiki/Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist">Methodist</a> parish church.</li>
<li><i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Andreaskirche</span></i> (St Andrew's Church) is a 14th-century Gothic parish church at Andrew's Street. The old craftsmen's quarter around it is named <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Andreasviertel</span></i> after the church.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/St._Augustine%27s_Monastery_(Erfurt)" title="St. Augustine's Monastery (Erfurt)">St. Augustine's Monastery</a> dates from 1277. <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> lived there as a monk between 1505 and 1511. The site has had a varied history and the restored complex has both modern and medieval buildings. Today it belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Church_in_Germany" title="Evangelical Church in Germany">Evangelical Church in Germany</a> and as well as being a place of worship it is also a meeting and conference centre, and provides simple guest accommodation. In 2016 an application was made for it to be included in the already existing UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> "Luther sites in Central Germany".<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Kaufmannskirche St. Gregor</span></i> (Merchant's Church St Gregory) is a 14th-century Gothic parish church at Anger Square. It is one of the largest and most important original parish churches in Erfurt. The parents of <a href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Johann Sebastian Bach">Johann Sebastian Bach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Ambrosius_Bach" title="Johann Ambrosius Bach">Johann Ambrosius Bach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maria_Elisabeth_L%C3%A4mmerhirt" title="Maria Elisabeth Lämmerhirt">Maria Elisabeth Lämmerhirt</a> married here in 1668.</li>
<li><i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Michaeliskirche</span></i> (St Michael's Church) is a 13th-century Gothic parish church in Michaelisstrasse. It became the church of the university in 1392.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Predigerkirche_(Erfurt)" title="Predigerkirche (Erfurt)">Predigerkirche</a></span></i> (Dominican Church) is a Gothic monastery church of the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Order" title="Dominican Order">Dominicans</a> at <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Prediger-straße</span>. Since the Reformation in the 16th century, it is the main Protestant church of Erfurt and furthermore one of the largest former churches of the mendicant orders in Germany. The theologian and mystic <a href="/wiki/Meister_Eckhart" title="Meister Eckhart">Meister Eckhart</a> (c. 1260 - 1328) entered Prediger Monastery around 1275. He was Prior from 1294 until 1298, and Vicar of Thuringia from 1298 to 1302. After a year in Paris, he returned to the monastery in 1303 and administered his duties as Provincial of Saxony from there until 1311.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup> The baroque composer <a href="/wiki/Johann_Pachelbel" title="Johann Pachelbel">Johann Pachelbel</a> (1653-1706) was organist at the church from 1678 until 1690.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Reglerkirche St. Augustinus</span></i> (Regulated St Augustine's Church) is a 12th-century Romanesque-Gothic monastery church of the Augustinians at Station Street. After the Reformation, it became a Protestant parish church.</li>
</ul>

<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_churches">Former churches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Former churches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<ul>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Barfüßerkirche</span></i> is a 14th-century Gothic monastery church at <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Barfüßer-straße</span></i>. The former <a href="/wiki/Franciscan" class="mw-redirect" title="Franciscan">Franciscan</a> monastery became a Protestant parish church after the Reformation. In 1944, the church was badly damaged by Allied bombing. Since that time its ruins have been preserved as a memorial against war and violence.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Bartholomäuskirche</span></i> (St Bartholomew's Church) was a parish church at Anger Square. The church was demolished before 1667 and only the steeple remained. Today, the steeple hosts a <a href="/wiki/Carillon" title="Carillon">carillon</a> with 60 bells.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Georgskirche</span></i> (St George's Church) was a parish church at Michael's Street. It was demolished in 1632 to yield construction material for the new citadel, and only the steeple remained.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Hospitalkirche</span></i> (Hospital Church) was the church of the former Great City Hospital at <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Juri-Gagarin-Ring</span></i>. It is a 14th-century Gothic building and now part of the museum of popular art and cultural anthropology.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Johanneskirche</span></i> (St John's Church) was a parish church at John's Street. It was demolished in 1819, but the steeple remained.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Kartäuserkirche St. Salvatorberg</span></i> (Carthusian Church, Mount St Saviour) was a monastery church at <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Kartäuser-straße</span></i>. The Baroque church was closed in 1803 and afterwards used for many different purposes. Today, it is part of a housing complex.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Nikolaikirche</span></i> (St Nicholas' Church) was a parish church in Augustine's Street. It was demolished in 1747 and only the steeple remained.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Paulskirche</span></i> (St Paul's Church) was a parish church in Paul's Street. It was demolished before 1759. The steeple remained and is in use as belfry of Preacher's Church.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Peterskirche</span></i> (St Peter's Church) was a monastery church at Petersberg hill. It was built in the 12th century in Romanesque style as church of the <a href="/wiki/Benedictine" class="mw-redirect" title="Benedictine">Benedictine</a> monastery. For its establishment 20 <a href="/wiki/Grivna" title="Grivna">grivna</a> of silver was donated by <a href="/wiki/Roman_the_Great" title="Roman the Great">Roman the Great</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> It was in use as a church until 1806. Later, it was part of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Petersberg_Citadel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Petersberg Citadel (page does not exist)">Petersberg Citadel</a> and reconstructed for military uses. In the process, the precious interior and furniture were lost. Today, St Peter's Church is a museum of concrete art.</li>
</ul>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">

</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">

<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Synagogues">Synagogues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Synagogues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The oldest parts of Erfurt's <i>Alte Synagoge</i> (<a href="/wiki/Old_Synagogue_(Erfurt)" title="Old Synagogue (Erfurt)">Old Synagogue</a>) date to the 11th century. It was used until 1349 when the Jewish community was destroyed in a pogrom known as the <a href="/wiki/Erfurt_massacre_(1349)" title="Erfurt massacre (1349)">Erfurt Massacre</a>. The building had many other uses since then. It was conserved in the 1990s and in 2009 it became a museum of Jewish history.<sup id="cite_ref-altsyn_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-altsyn-42">[40]</a></sup> A rare <a href="/wiki/Mikveh" title="Mikveh">Mikveh</a>, a ritual bath, dating from c.1250, was discovered by archeologists in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-mikveh_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mikveh-12">[11]</a></sup> It has been accessible to visitors on guided tours since September 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> In 2015 the Old Synagogue and Mikveh were nominated as a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>. It has been tentatively listed but a final decision has not yet been made.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>As religious freedom was granted in the 19th century, some Jews returned to Erfurt. They built their synagogue on the banks of the Gera river and used it from 1840 until 1884. The neoclassical building is known as the <i>Kleine Synagoge</i> (Small Synagogue). Today it is used an events centre. It is also open to visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-kleinsyn_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kleinsyn-56">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>A larger synagogue, the <i>Große Synagoge</i> (Great Synagogue), was opened in 1884 because the community had become larger and wealthier. This moorish style building was destroyed during nationwide Nazi riots, known as <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Kristallnacht" title="Kristallnacht">Kristallnacht</a></span> on 9–10 November 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1947 the land which the Great Synagogue had occupied was returned to the Jewish community and they built their current place of worship, the <i>Neue Synagoge</i> (New Synagogue) which opened in 1952. It was the only synagogue building erected under communist rule in East Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Secular_architecture">Secular architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Secular architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Besides the religious buildings there is a lot of historic secular architecture in Erfurt, mostly concentrated in the city centre, but some 19th- and 20th-century buildings are located on the outskirts.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Michaelisstra%C3%9Fe_Erfurt.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Michaelisstra%C3%9Fe_Erfurt.JPG/220px-Michaelisstra%C3%9Fe_Erfurt.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Michaelisstra%C3%9Fe_Erfurt.JPG/330px-Michaelisstra%C3%9Fe_Erfurt.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Michaelisstra%C3%9Fe_Erfurt.JPG/440px-Michaelisstra%C3%9Fe_Erfurt.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2803" data-file-height="3733" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Michaelisstra%C3%9Fe_Erfurt.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Michaelisstraße</span> is known as the lithic chronicle of Erfurt</div>
</div>
</div>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Street_and_square_ensembles">Street and square ensembles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Street and square ensembles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<ul>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Kr%C3%A4merbr%C3%BCcke" title="Krämerbrücke">Krämerbrücke</a></span></i> (Merchants' bridge) is the most famous tourist attraction of Erfurt. This 15th-century bridge is completely covered with dwellings and unique in Europe north of the Alps. Today, there are some art handicraft and souvenir shops in the houses.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Domplatz</span></i> (Cathedral Square) is the largest square in Erfurt and one of the largest historical market squares in Germany. The cathedral and St Severus' Church on its western side can be reached over the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Domstufen</span></i>, a wide flight of stairs. On the north side lies the courthouse, a historic building from 1880. The eastern and southern side is fronted by early-modern patrician houses. On the square are the Minerva Fountain from 1784 and the Erthal Obelisk from 1777. The Domplatz is the main setting of the Erfurt Christmas Market in December and the location for "DomStufen-Festival", an open-air theatre festival in summer.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Fischmarkt</span></i> (Fish Market) is the central square of Erfurt's city centre. It is surrounded by renaissance-style patrician houses and the town hall, a neo-gothic building from 1882. In the middle of the square is a statue called <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Römer</span></i> (Roman), a symbol of the city's independence, erected by the citizens in 1591.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Wenigemarkt</span></i> (Minor Market) is a small square on the east side of the Gera river (opposite to the Fischmarkt on the west side), surrounded by early-modern patrician and merchants' houses. The fountain on this square with the sculpture "Scuffling Boys" was created in 1975. Today, <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Wenigemarkt</span> square also has various cafés and bars. Next to the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Wenigemarkt</span> in <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Futterstraße</span> is the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Kaisersaal</span> building, a neoclassicistic event hall from 1831 (current building). The <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Erfurt" title="Congress of Erfurt">Congress of Erfurt</a> took place here in 1808.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Anger</span></i> (originally the German term for "<a href="/wiki/Village_green" title="Village green">village green</a>") is a protracted square<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (October 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> in the eastern city centre. All tram lines are linked here, so that it became the new city centre during the 20th century with many important buildings. On its northern side is the main post office, built in 1886 in neo-gothic style with its prominent clock tower. In the north-east there is the Martin Luther monument from 1889 in front of the Merchants' Church. Between the church and the Ursuline monastery lies the "Anger 1" department store from 1908. On the south side next to Station Street is the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Angermuseum</span>, the art history museum of Erfurt, inside a Baroque palace from 1711. The western part of Anger square is surrounded by large historicist business houses from the late 19th century. The west end of the square is marked by the Angerbrunnen fountain from 1890. The Jesuit College near <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Schlösserstraße</span> was built in 1737 and used until the ban of the Jesuits in 1773.</li>
<li>The <i><a href="/wiki/Willy_Brandt" title="Willy Brandt">Willy Brandt</a> Square</i> is the southern gate to the city centre in front of the main station. Opposite to the station is the former hotel <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Erfurter Hof</span></i>, where the first meeting of the East- and West-German heads of government took place in 1970. On the western side is the building of the old Erfurt station (1847–95) with a clock tower and the former offices of the Thuringian Railway Company.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Hirschgarten</span></i> (Deer Garden) is a small park in front of the Thuringian government seat in the western city centre. The minister-president's seat is the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Kurmainzische Statthalterei</span></i>, a Renaissance-Baroque palace from the 17th century.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Michaelisstraße</span></i> (Michael's Street) is known as "the lithic chronicle of Erfurt", because of its mostly medieval buildings. It is the main street of the Latin quarter around the old university and today one of the favourite nightlife districts of the Erfurters with various bars, restaurants and cafés. The central building of the old university, <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">Collegium Maius</span>, was built in 1515, destroyed by Allied bombs in 1945 and originally rebuilt in 1999.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Juri-Gagarin-Ring</span></i> is an inner-city circular road following the former inner city wall. The road was set out in the 1890s by closing a branch of the Gera river. The buildings along the street originate from all periods of the 20th century, including some GDR-era highrise residence buildings. An old building complex here is the former Great Hospital, established in the 14th century. Today, it hosts the museum of popular art and cultural anthropology.</li>
<li>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Andreasviertel</span></i> (St Andrew's Quarter) is a small quarter in the northern part of the city centre between <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Domplatz</span> in the south-west and <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Moritzwallstraße</span> in the north-east. It was the former craftsmen quarter with narrow alleys and old (16th/17th century) little houses. During the 20th century, there were plans to demolish the quarter because of its bad housing conditions. After 1990, the houses were redeveloped by private individuals so that it is one of the favourite neighbourhoods today. The largest building here is the former Municipal Corn Storage in Gothic style from 1466 with a floor area of 1,800&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (19,375&#160;sq&#160;ft).</li>
</ul>

<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Fortifications">Fortifications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Fortifications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LuftbildPetersberg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/LuftbildPetersberg.jpg/220px-LuftbildPetersberg.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/LuftbildPetersberg.jpg/330px-LuftbildPetersberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/LuftbildPetersberg.jpg/440px-LuftbildPetersberg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1158" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LuftbildPetersberg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Petersberg Citadel</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Fortifications played an important role during Erfurt's history. Nevertheless, the city wall was broken down in 1873. There are only a few remains of the walls today, for example the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Johannesmauer</span></i> near <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Franckestraße</span> in the north-east of the city centre. More important are the two early-modern citadels of Erfurt, which remain more or less in their original state.</p>
<p>The Petersberg Citadel is one of the largest extant early-modern citadels in Europe and covers the whole north-western part of the city centre. It was built after 1665 on Petersberg hill and was in military use until 1963. Since 1990, it has been renovated, but in parts is still not finished.</p>
<p>The Cyriaksburg Citadel is a smaller early-modern citadel south-west of the city centre, built during the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>. Today, it hosts the German horticultural museum.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="19th-_and_20th-century_architecture_in_the_outskirts">19th- and 20th-century architecture in the outskirts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: 19th- and 20th-century architecture in the outskirts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Between 1873 and 1914, a belt of <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCnderzeit" title="Gründerzeit">Gründerzeit</a></span></i> architecture emerged around the city centre. The mansion district in the south-west around <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Cyriakstraße</span>, <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Richard-Breslau-Straße</span> and <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Hochheimer Straße</span> hosts some interesting <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Gründerzeit</span></i> and <i>Art Nouveau</i> buildings.</p>
<p>The "Mühlenviertel" ("mill quarter"), is an area of beautiful Art Nouveau apartment buildings, cobblestone streets and street trees just to the north of the old city, in the vicinity of Nord Park, bordered by the Gera river on its east side. The "Schmale Gera" stream runs through the area. In the Middle Ages numerous small enterprises using the power of water mills occupied the area, hence the name "Mühlenviertel", with street names such as Waidmühlenweg (woad, or indigo, mill way), Storchmühlenweg (stork mill way) and Papiermühlenweg (paper mill way).</p>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Bauhaus" title="Bauhaus">Bauhaus</a></i> style is represented by some housing cooperative projects in the east around <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Flensburger Straße</span> and <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Dortmunder Straße</span> and in the north around <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Neuendorfstraße</span>. Lutherkirke Church in <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Magdeburger Allee</span> (1927), is an <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a> building.</p>
<p>The former malt factory "Wolff" at <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Theo-Neubauer-Straße</span> in the east of Erfurt is a large industrial complex built between 1880 and 1939, and in use until 2000. A new use has not been found yet, but the area is sometimes used as a location in movie productions because of its atmosphere.</p>
<p>Some examples of Nazi architecture are the buildings of the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Landtag</span> (Thuringian parliament) and <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Thüringenhalle</span> (an event hall) in the south at <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Arnstädter Straße</span>. While the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Landtag</span> building (1930s) represents more the neo-Roman/fascist style, <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Thüringenhalle</span> (1940s) is marked by some neo-Germanic <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Heimatschutz</span></i> style elements.</p>
<p>The Stalinist early-GDR style is manifested in the main building of the university at <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Nordhäuser Straße</span> (1953) and the later more international modern GDR style is represented by the horticultural exhibition centre "<span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Egapark</span>" at <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Gothaer Straße</span>, the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Plattenbau</span> housing complexes like Rieth or <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Johannesplatz</span> and the redevelopment of <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Löbertor</span> and <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Krämpfertor</span> area along <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Juri-Gagarin-Ring</span> in the city centre.</p>
<p>The current international glass and steel architecture is dominant among most larger new buildings like the Federal Labour Court of Germany (1999), the new opera house (2003), the new main station (2007), the university library, the Erfurt Messe (convention centre) and the <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Gunda_Niemann-Stirnemann" title="Gunda Niemann-Stirnemann">Gunda Niemann-Stirnemann</a></span> ice rink.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_and_infrastructure">Economy and infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Economy and infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>During recent years, the economic situation of the city improved: the unemployment rate declined from 21% in 2005 to 9% in 2013. Nevertheless, some 14,000 households with 24,500 persons (12% of population) are dependent upon state social benefits (<a href="/wiki/Hartz_concept" title="Hartz concept">Hartz IV</a>).</p>
<h3><span id="Agriculture,_industry_and_services"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture.2C_industry_and_services">Agriculture, industry and services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Agriculture, industry and services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Optima-Werk_Erfurt.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Optima-Werk_Erfurt.JPG/220px-Optima-Werk_Erfurt.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Optima-Werk_Erfurt.JPG/330px-Optima-Werk_Erfurt.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Optima-Werk_Erfurt.JPG/440px-Optima-Werk_Erfurt.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Optima-Werk_Erfurt.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Former factory building, now reused for services</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Anger_1_Erfurt_Kaufhaus_R%C3%B6mischer_Kaiser_686-vLh.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Anger_1_Erfurt_Kaufhaus_R%C3%B6mischer_Kaiser_686-vLh.jpg/220px-Anger_1_Erfurt_Kaufhaus_R%C3%B6mischer_Kaiser_686-vLh.jpg" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Anger_1_Erfurt_Kaufhaus_R%C3%B6mischer_Kaiser_686-vLh.jpg/330px-Anger_1_Erfurt_Kaufhaus_R%C3%B6mischer_Kaiser_686-vLh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Anger_1_Erfurt_Kaufhaus_R%C3%B6mischer_Kaiser_686-vLh.jpg/440px-Anger_1_Erfurt_Kaufhaus_R%C3%B6mischer_Kaiser_686-vLh.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1185" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Anger_1_Erfurt_Kaufhaus_R%C3%B6mischer_Kaiser_686-vLh.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Anger 1</i>, a big department store in centre</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Farming has a great tradition in Erfurt: the cultivation of <a href="/wiki/Isatis_tinctoria" title="Isatis tinctoria">woad</a> made the city rich during the Middle Ages. Today, horticulture and the production of flower seeds is still an important business in Erfurt. There is also growing of fruits (like apples, strawberries and sweet cherries), vegetables (e.g. cauliflowers, potatoes, cabbage and sugar beets) and grain on more than 60% of the municipal territory.</p>
<p>Industrialization in Erfurt started around 1850. Until World War I, many factories were founded in different sectors like engine building, shoes, guns, malt and later electro-technics, so that there was no industrial monoculture in the city. After 1945, the companies were nationalized by the <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">GDR</a> government, which led to the decline of some of them. After reunification, nearly all factories were closed, either because they failed to successfully adopt to a free market economy or because the German government sold them to west German businessmen who closed them to avoid competition to their own enterprises.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> However, in the early 1990s the federal government started to subsidize the foundation of new companies. It still took a long time before the economic situation stabilized around 2006. Since this time, unemployment has decreased and overall, new jobs were created. Today, there are many small and medium-sized companies in Erfurt with electro-technics, semiconductors and photovoltaics in focus. Building engines, the production of food (i.e. a big noodle factory), the <a href="/wiki/Braugold" title="Braugold">Braugold</a> brewery, and <a href="/wiki/Born_Feinkost" title="Born Feinkost">Born Feinkost</a> a producer of Thuringian mustard, are still an important industries.</p>
<p>Erfurt is an <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Oberzentrum</span></i> (which means "supra-centre" according to <a href="/wiki/Central_place_theory" title="Central place theory">Central place theory</a>) in German regional planning. Such centres are always hubs of service businesses and public services like hospitals, universities, research, trade fairs, retail etc. Additionally, Erfurt is the capital of the federal state of Thuringia, so that there are many institutions of administration like all the Thuringian state ministries and some nationwide authorities. Typical for Erfurt are the logistic business with many distribution centres of big companies, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt_Trade_Fair&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Erfurt Trade Fair (page does not exist)">Erfurt Trade Fair</a> and the media sector with <a href="/wiki/KiKa" title="KiKa">KiKa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mitteldeutscher_Rundfunk" title="Mitteldeutscher Rundfunk">MDR</a> as public broadcast stations. A growing industry is tourism, due to the various historical sights of Erfurt. There are 4,800 hotel beds and (in 2012) 450,000 overnight visitors spent a total of 700,000 nights in hotels. Nevertheless, most tourists are one-day visitors from Germany. The Christmas Market in December attracts some 2,000,000 visitors each year.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Erfurt_Hbf_Front.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Erfurt_Hbf_Front.JPG/220px-Erfurt_Hbf_Front.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Erfurt_Hbf_Front.JPG/330px-Erfurt_Hbf_Front.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Erfurt_Hbf_Front.JPG/440px-Erfurt_Hbf_Front.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Erfurt_Hbf_Front.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Erfurt_Hauptbahnhof" title="Erfurt Hauptbahnhof">Erfurt Hauptbahnhof</a>, Erfurt's main railway station.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="By_rail">By rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: By rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" title="Intercity-Express">ICE</a> railway network makes Erfurt 1½ hours from <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, 2 hours from <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a>, and 45 minutes from <a href="/wiki/Leipzig" title="Leipzig">Leipzig</a>. In 2017 the ICE line to <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> will open, making the trip to Erfurt only 2 hours.</p>
<p>There are regional trains from Erfurt to <a href="/wiki/Weimar" title="Weimar">Weimar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jena" title="Jena">Jena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gotha" title="Gotha">Gotha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eisenach" title="Eisenach">Eisenach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bad_Langensalza" title="Bad Langensalza">Bad Langensalza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magdeburg" title="Magdeburg">Magdeburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nordhausen" title="Nordhausen">Nordhausen</a>, <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6ttingen" title="Göttingen">Göttingen</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BChlhausen" title="Mühlhausen">Mühlhausen</a>, <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrzburg" title="Würzburg">Würzburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meiningen" title="Meiningen">Meiningen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilmenau" title="Ilmenau">Ilmenau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arnstadt" title="Arnstadt">Arnstadt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gera" title="Gera">Gera</a> .</p>
<p>In freight transport there is an <a href="/wiki/Intermodal_freight_transport" title="Intermodal freight transport">intermodal</a> terminal in the district of Vieselbach <i>(<span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Güterverkehrszentrum, GVZ</span>)</i> with connections to rail and the autobahn.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="By_road">By road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: By road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The two <a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">Autobahnen</a> crossing each other nearby at <i>Erfurter Kreuz</i> are the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_4" title="Bundesautobahn 4">Bundesautobahn 4</a> (<a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>–<a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_71" title="Bundesautobahn 71">Bundesautobahn 71</a> (<a href="/wiki/Schweinfurt" title="Schweinfurt">Schweinfurt</a>–<a href="/wiki/Sangerhausen" title="Sangerhausen">Sangerhausen</a>). Together with the east tangent both motorways form a circle road around the city and lead the interregional traffic around the centre. Whereas the A 4 was built in the 1930s, the A 71 came into being after the reunification in the 1990s and 2000s. In addition to both motorways there are two <a href="/wiki/Bundesstra%C3%9Fe" title="Bundesstraße">Bundesstraßen</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Bundesstra%C3%9Fe_7" title="Bundesstraße 7">Bundesstraße 7</a> connects Erfurt parallel to A 4 with <a href="/wiki/Gotha" title="Gotha">Gotha</a> in the west and <a href="/wiki/Weimar" title="Weimar">Weimar</a> in the east. The <a href="/wiki/Bundesstra%C3%9Fe_4" title="Bundesstraße 4">Bundesstraße 4</a> is a connection between Erfurt and <a href="/wiki/Nordhausen" title="Nordhausen">Nordhausen</a> in the north. Its southern part to <a href="/wiki/Coburg" title="Coburg">Coburg</a> was annulled when A 71 was finished (in this section, the A 71 now effectively serves as B 4). Within the circle road, B 7 and B 4 are also annulled, so that the city government has to pay for maintenance instead of the German federal government. The access to the city is restricted as <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Low-emission_zone" title="Low-emission zone">Umweltzone</a></span></i> since 2012 for some vehicles. Large parts of the inner city are a pedestrian area which can not be reached by car (except for residents).</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="By_light_rail_and_bus">By light rail and bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: By light rail and bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Erfurt_Stra%C3%9Fenbahn_Schl%C3%B6sserstr.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Erfurt_Stra%C3%9Fenbahn_Schl%C3%B6sserstr.JPG/220px-Erfurt_Stra%C3%9Fenbahn_Schl%C3%B6sserstr.JPG" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Erfurt_Stra%C3%9Fenbahn_Schl%C3%B6sserstr.JPG/330px-Erfurt_Stra%C3%9Fenbahn_Schl%C3%B6sserstr.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Erfurt_Stra%C3%9Fenbahn_Schl%C3%B6sserstr.JPG/440px-Erfurt_Stra%C3%9Fenbahn_Schl%C3%B6sserstr.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3456" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Erfurt_Stra%C3%9Fenbahn_Schl%C3%B6sserstr.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Light rail tram near Anger square</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Erfurt public transport system is marked by the area-wide <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Erfurt_Stadtbahn" title="Erfurt Stadtbahn">Erfurt Stadtbahn</a></span> (<a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a>) network, established as a tram system in 1883, upgraded to a light rail ( <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Stadtbahn</span></i> ) system in 1997,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup> and continually expanded and upgraded through the 2000s. Today, there are six <i>Stadtbahn</i> lines running every ten minutes on every light rail route.</p>
<p>Additionally, Erfurt operates a bus system, which connects the sparsely populated outer districts of the region to the city center. Both systems are organized by <i>SWE EVAG</i>, a transit company owned by the city administration. Trolleybuses were in service in Erfurt from 1948 until 1975, but are no longer in service.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="By_airplane">By airplane</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: By airplane">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Erfurt-Weimar_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Erfurt-Weimar Airport">Erfurt-Weimar Airport</a> lies 3&#160;km (2&#160;mi) west of the city centre. It is linked to the central train station via Stadtbahn (tram). It was significantly extended in the 1990s, with flights mostly to Mediterranean holiday destinations and to London during the peak Christmas market tourist season. Connections to longer haul flights are easily accessible via <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a>, which can be reached in 2 hours via a direct train from Frankfurt Airport to Erfurt, and from <a href="/wiki/Leipzig_Halle_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Leipzig Halle Airport">Leipzig/Halle Airport</a>, which can be reached within half an hour.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="By_bike">By bike</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: By bike">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Biking is becoming increasingly popular since construction of high quality cycle tracks began in the 1990s. There are cycle lanes for general commuting within Erfurt city.</p>
<p>Long-distance trails, such as the <i>Gera track</i> and the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Radweg Thüringer Städtekette</span></i> (Thuringian cities trail), connect points of tourist interest. The former runs along the <a href="/wiki/Gera_(river)" title="Gera (river)">Gera</a> river valley from the <a href="/wiki/Thuringian_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Thuringian forest">Thuringian forest</a> to the river <a href="/wiki/Unstrut" title="Unstrut">Unstrut</a>; the latter follows the medieval <a href="/wiki/Via_Regia" title="Via Regia">Via Regia</a> from <a href="/wiki/Eisenach" title="Eisenach">Eisenach</a> to <a href="/wiki/Altenburg" title="Altenburg">Altenburg</a> via <a href="/wiki/Gotha" title="Gotha">Gotha</a>, Erfurt, <a href="/wiki/Weimar" title="Weimar">Weimar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jena" title="Jena">Jena</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rennsteig_Cycle_Way" class="mw-redirect" title="Rennsteig Cycle Way">Rennsteig Cycle Way</a> was opened in 2000. This designated high-grade hiking and bike trail runs along the ridge of the Thuringian Central Uplands. The bike trail, about 200&#160;km (124&#160;mi) long, occasionally departs from the course of the historic Rennsteig hiking trail, which dates back to the 1300s, to avoid steep inclines. It is therefore about 30&#160;km (19&#160;mi) longer than the hiking trail.</p>
<p>The Rennsteig is connected to the <a href="/wiki/E3_European_long_distance_path" title="E3 European long distance path">E3 European long distance path</a>, which goes from the Atlantic coast of Spain to the Black Sea coast of Bulgaria, and the <a href="/wiki/E6_European_long_distance_path" title="E6 European long distance path">E6 European long distance path</a>, running from Arctic Finland to Turkey.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After reunification, the educational system was reorganized. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Erfurt" title="University of Erfurt">University of Erfurt</a>, founded in 1379<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-14">[13]</a></sup> and closed in 1816, was refounded in 1994 with a focus on social sciences, modern languages, humanities and teacher training. Today there are approximately 6,000 students working within four faculties, the Max Weber Center for Advanced Cultural and Social Studies, and three academic research institutes.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> The University has an international reputation and participates in international student exchange programmes.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Fachhochschule Erfurt</i>, is a <a href="/wiki/Fachhochschule" title="Fachhochschule">university of applied sciences</a>, founded in 1991, which offers a combination of academic training and practical experience in subjects such as social work and social pedagogy, business studies, and engineering. There are nearly 5,000 students in six faculties, of which the faculty of landscaping and horticulture has a national reputation.</p>
<p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adam-Ries-Fachhochschule&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Adam-Ries-Fachhochschule (page does not exist)">Adam-Ries-Fachhochschule</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adam-Ries-Fachhochschule" class="extiw" title="de:Adam-Ries-Fachhochschule">de</a>)</span> is a privately run university of applied sciences, founded in 2008, with a focus on business and economics.</p>
<p>The world renowned <a href="/wiki/Bauhaus" title="Bauhaus">Bauhaus</a> design school was founded in 1919 in the city of <a href="/wiki/Weimar" title="Weimar">Weimar</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> approximately 20&#160;km (12&#160;mi) from Erfurt, 12 minutes by train. The buildings are now part of a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> and are today used by the <a href="/wiki/Bauhaus-Universit%C3%A4t_Weimar" class="mw-redirect" title="Bauhaus-Universität Weimar">Bauhaus-Universität Weimar</a>, which teaches design, arts, media and technology related subjects.</p>
<p>Furthermore, there are eight <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(Germany)" title="Gymnasium (Germany)">Gymnasien</a></span></i>, six state-owned, one Catholic and one Protestant. One of the state-owned schools is a <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Sportgymnasium</span></i>, an elite boarding school for young talents in athletics, swimming, ice skating or football. Another state-owned school, <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Albert Schweitzer Gymnasium</span></i>, offers a focus in sciences as an elite boarding school in addition to the common curriculum.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The German national public television children’s channel <i>KiKa</i> is based in Erfurt.</p>
<p>MDR (Mittel Deutschland Rundfunk), a radio and television company, has a broadcast centre and studios in Erfurt.</p>
<p>The <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Th%C3%BCringer_Allgemeine" title="Thüringer Allgemeine">Thüringer Allgemeine</a></span></i>, a newspaper, is headquartered in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mayor_and_city_council">Mayor and city council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Mayor and city council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first freely elected mayor after German reunification was <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manfred_Ruge&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Manfred Ruge (page does not exist)">Manfred Ruge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Union_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian Democratic Union (Germany)">CDU</a> (in office from 1990 to 2006), followed by <a href="/wiki/Andreas_Bausewein" title="Andreas Bausewein">Andreas Bausewein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">SPD</a> (in office since 2006).</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns">Twin towns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Twin towns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Germany" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Germany">List of twin towns and sister cities in Germany</a></div>

<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali"><img alt="Mali" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Mali.svg/23px-Flag_of_Mali.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Mali.svg/35px-Flag_of_Mali.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Mali.svg/45px-Flag_of_Mali.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="300" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Kati" class="mw-redirect" title="Kati">Kati</a>, Mali (2011)<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Bowling_Green,_Kentucky" title="Bowling Green, Kentucky">Bowling Green, Kentucky</a>, United States</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People_from_Erfurt">People from Erfurt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: People from Erfurt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><i>See: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Erfurt" title="List of people from Erfurt">List of people from Erfurt</a></i></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Erfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Footnotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As with the case of an <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphism#Examples_in_prehistory" title="Anthropomorphism">anthropomorhic</a> figurine excavated in Erfurt, some researchers including Olaf Höckmann<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> indicated those were intentionally broken, since neolithic figurines in human figure were found in fragment in high ratio among excavations in central Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Between 1631 and 1648, during the Thirty Years’ War, Erfurt was occupied by Swedish forces,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> thus the <a href="/wiki/Effigy" title="Effigy">effigy</a> of Queen Christina appears on the 1645 Erfurt 10 <a href="/wiki/Ducat" title="Ducat">Ducat</a> (Portugaloser). There are seven gold coins known to exist bearing the effigy of Queen Christina: a unique 1649 five ducat,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> and six 1645 10 ducat specimen.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>
</div>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;"></div>

<li id="cite_note-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-8"><sup><i><b>i</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-9"><sup><i><b>j</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-10"><sup><i><b>k</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-11"><sup><i><b>l</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-12"><sup><i><b>m</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Erfurt_Chronik_1806.E2.80.931814_23-13"><sup><i><b>n</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.erfurt.de/ef/de/erleben/entdecken/geschichte/chronik/111885.html">"1806–1814: Erfurt unter französischer Besetzung"</a> [1806–1814: Erfurt under French occupation] (in German). Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2 January</span> 2016</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AErfurt&amp;rft.btitle=1806%E2%80%931814%3A+Erfurt+unter+franz%C3%B6sischer+Besetzung&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.pub=Erfurt+Stadtverwaltung+%5BErfurt+city+administration%5D&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.erfurt.de%2Fef%2Fde%2Ferleben%2Fentdecken%2Fgeschichte%2Fchronik%2F111885.html&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-F.C3.BCrstenkongress-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-F.C3.BCrstenkongress_24-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-F.C3.BCrstenkongress_24-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-F.C3.BCrstenkongress_24-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.erfurter-fuerstenkongress-1808.de/historie.htm">"Kurzer historischer Überblick"</a> [Brief historical overview]. <i>Napoleon's Fürstenkongress Erfurt</i> (in German). Euratibor<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2 January</span> 2016</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AErfurt&amp;rft.atitle=Kurzer+historischer+%C3%9Cberblick&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Napoleon%27s+F%C3%BCrstenkongress+Erfurt&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.erfurter-fuerstenkongress-1808.de%2Fhistorie.htm&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-25">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Gerhard Robert Walter von Coeckelberghe-Dützele (1834). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.co.uk/books?id=upBXAAAAcAAJ&amp;pg=PA21"><i>Ruinen oder Taschenbuch zur Geschichte verfallener Ritterburgen und Schlößer (etc.)</i></a> [<i>Ruins, or: A pocketbook on the history of dilapidated knights' castles</i>] (in German). Mich. Lechner. p.&#160;21<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">23 January</span> 2016</span>. <q><i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Nach der unglücklichen Schlacht bei Jena und dem Rückzuge der Preußen, wurde sie durch Kapitulation den Franzosen übergeben, und erhielt anfangs eine ziemlich starke Besatzung; doch wurde sie in der Folge so von ihnen vernachläßigt, daß in einer gewissen Epoche der Marketender Sturm mit seiner Familie und ein alter Unteroffizier ihre ganze Garnison ausmachten. Damals war es, wo der Intendant Devismes und der Domainen-Direktor Gentil in der nach der Stadt zugekehrten Seite der Mauer einen Schatz suchen ließ, der noch aus den Zeiten des ehemaligen Benedektiner-Nonnenklosters hier versteckt seyn sollte, ohne zu bedenken, daß zufolge der oben angeführten, an der Mauer befindlichen Inschrift, kein Schatz von 1478 her in einer Mauer versteckt seyn konnte, die über 100 Jahre darnach erst erbaut worden war; aber die Habsucht eilte hier jeder nähern Untersuchung vor. Bei dieser Gelegenheit wurde auch die alte Burgkapelle demoliert und aus den verkauften Baumaterialien die Arbeiter bezahlt, die beim Schatzgraben hilfreiche Hand geleistet hatten.</span></i> [After the unfortunate battle of Jena and the retreat of the Prussians, it was handed over by capitulation to the French, and was initially fairly strongly garrisoned; but was subsequently so neglected that at one time the whole garrison consisted of the <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/sutler" class="extiw" title="wikt:sutler">sutler</a> Sturm with his family and an old sergeant. At that time, Intendant <a href="/w/index.php?title=De_Vismes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="De Vismes (page does not exist)">de Vismes</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pierre_Jean_Louis_de_Vismes" class="extiw" title="fr:Pierre Jean Louis de Vismes">fr</a>)</span> and Domain-Director Gentil searched in the city-side walls for treasure hidden since the times of the former Benedictine nunnery — without considering that an inscription located on the wall above showed that it had been built just over 100 years later, so no treasure could have been hidden there in 1478, but greed hastened this before any closer investigation. On that occasion the old chapel was demolished, and the workers who had helped dig for treasure were paid from the sale of the building materials.]</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AErfurt&amp;rft.au=Gerhard+Robert+Walter+von+Coeckelberghe-D%C3%BCtzele&amp;rft.btitle=Ruinen+oder+Taschenbuch+zur+Geschichte+verfallener+Ritterburgen+und+Schl%C3%B6%C3%9Fer+%28etc.%29&amp;rft.date=1834&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.pages=21&amp;rft.pub=Mich.+Lechner&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.co.uk%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DupBXAAAAcAAJ%26pg%3DPA21&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Denkmale_Erfurts-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Denkmale_Erfurts_26-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Denkmale_Erfurts_26-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Denkmale_Erfurts_26-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Denkmale_Erfurts_26-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Denkmale_Erfurts_26-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.thueringer-naturbrief.de/index.php?option=com_content&amp;task=view&amp;id=97&amp;Itemid=187&amp;limit=1&amp;limitstart=5">"Denkmale Erfurts 1806–1814"</a> [Monuments of Erfurt 1806–1814] (in German). Thüringer Naturbrief<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">3 January</span> 2016</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AErfurt&amp;rft.btitle=Denkmale+Erfurts+1806%E2%80%931814&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.pub=Th%C3%BCringer+Naturbrief&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.thueringer-naturbrief.de%2Findex.php%3Foption%3Dcom_content%26task%3Dview%26id%3D97%26Itemid%3D187%26limit%3D1%26limitstart%3D5&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-Koch-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Koch_29-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Koch_29-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/Christoph_Wilhelm_von_Koch" title="Christoph Wilhelm von Koch">Christoph Wilhelm von Koch</a> (1838). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.co.uk/books?id=7lw_AAAAcAAJ&amp;pg=PA303"><i>Histoire abrégée des traités de paix entre les puissances de l'Europe depuis la paix de Westphalie, Volume 3</i></a> [<i>Abridged history of the peace treaties between the powers of Europe since the Peace of Westphalia, Volume 3</i>] (in French). Meline, Cans et Compagnie. <q><i><span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr">Le général Kleist assiégeait Erfurt. Par suite d'une capitulation signée le 20 décembre, le générale français d'Alton se retira dans les deux forts de Petersberg et Cyriacsbourg, et la ville fut remise aux Prussiens le 6 janvier 1814.</span></i> [General Kleist laid siege to Erfurt. As a result of a capitulation signed on 20 December, the French general d'Alton withdrew to the two forts of Petersberg and Cyriaksburg, and the town was handed over to the Prussians on 6 January 1814.]</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AErfurt&amp;rft.au=Christoph+Wilhelm+von+Koch&amp;rft.btitle=Histoire+abr%C3%A9g%C3%A9e+des+trait%C3%A9s+de+paix+entre+les+puissances+de+l%27Europe+depuis+la+paix+de+Westphalie%2C+Volume+3&amp;rft.date=1838&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.pub=Meline%2C+Cans+et+Compagnie&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.co.uk%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D7lw_AAAAcAAJ%26pg%3DPA303&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-H.C3.BChn_1839-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-H.C3.BChn_1839_31-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-H.C3.BChn_1839_31-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite id="CITEREFGeorg_Friedrich_H.C3.BChn1839" class="citation">Georg Friedrich Hühn (1839), <i>Kurzgefasste Nachricht von der Belagerung, Blokade und Einzug der Königlich Preußischen Truppen in Erfurt. Vom 21sten Oktober 1813 bis zum 8ten Januar 1814. In einem Briefe als ein Journal abgefasst, und an einen vertrauten Freund abgesendet. Bei Gelegenheit der 25jährigen Jubelfeier neu abgedruckt</i> [<i>Concise news of the siege, blockade and entry of the Royal Prussian troops into Erfurt. From 21 October 1813 to 8 January 1814. In a letter as a journal written and sent to a trusted friend.
